<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1264098991">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1264098991" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/19138848-noe" class="left imgcol" title="Noe"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442883462p2/19138848.jpg" alt="Noe" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1264098991?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 02, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/19138848-noe" class="user" title="Noe">Noe</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6058948-the-convenient-marriage" title="Paperback 9781402217722" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1264098991">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16849159956609522891">Ms. Heyer has a very funny sense of humor and a real talent for putting it down on paper, and in this book there were times I laughed almost through a whole chapter. However, to me it seemed she was trying to tell two stories and did a poor job on one and just fair on the other.<br /><br />Considering the title, one would think she was trying to write a romance novel of sorts, and this is where she really blew it, because she had the makings of a real good love story. The Earl of Rule accepts the offer of s</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16849159956609522891">Ms. Heyer has a very funny sense of humor and a real talent for putting it down on paper, and in this book there were times I laughed almost through a whole chapter. However, to me it seemed she was trying to tell two stories and did a poor job on one and just fair on the other.<br /><br />Considering the title, one would think she was trying to write a romance novel of sorts, and this is where she really blew it, because she had the makings of a real good love story. The Earl of Rule accepts the offer of seventeen-year-old Horatia to take the place of her older sister to marry him because her older sister is already in love with someone else. Those of you who have read the book might say since the Earl falls in love with Horatia at the end, it is a sweet love story, but the problem is the author doesn’t have the Earl and Horatia together enough to show how or why they fall in love.<br /><br />Instead, immediately after the marriage Horatia becomes this whole different character that seemed to have maneuvered everything so she can live the high life. The sweet innocent girl that was willing to sacrifice herself for her sister’s love is no longer seen and a rather wild and extravagant person takes her place. The turn of her character made no sense and is another reason that makes the Earl falling in love with her hard to accept, since she is spending unbelievable amounts of money on clothes and jewel-encrusted shoes and racking up huge gambling debts. A romance is not seen in any of these goings on.<br /><br />If Ms. Heyer would have just focused on writing a comedy about Horatia’s brother the Viscount, who, by the way, takes up a great deal of the book anyway and is the other story that is being told, it would have been a much better book. She could have called it something like ‘How to Defend Your Sister’s Honor and other Adventures of a Viscount.’<br /><br />What we have, though, is a story that limps along in its hodge-podge way, leaving me wishing the author had chosen to write one or the other story. It is not that a book can’t have two stories going on at the same time, but if it is to be done, both story lines need to be developed sufficiently so that it all makes sense.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16849159956609522891">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_135805981">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/135805981" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart" class="left imgcol" title="Jane Stewart"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1346001994p2/3789528.jpg" alt="Jane Stewart" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/135805981?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 20, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart" class="user" title="Jane Stewart">Jane Stewart</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/8516495-the-convenient-marriage" title=" 9781408490372" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3789528-jane-stewart?shelf=historical-romance" class="actionLinkLite">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3789528-jane-stewart?shelf=georgian-romance" class="actionLinkLite">georgian-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer135805981">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2858717517358904578">Really interesting characters. Fun scrapes and schemes. I didn’t want to stop reading. I was eager for them to fall in love.<br /><br />STORY BRIEF:<br />I excerpted much of the following from the website Heyerlist dot org which says it well – what to expect when you read this book.<br /><br />The Earl of Rule (Rule) is 35, proud, wealthy. He has a pleasant, mocking, lazy charm which belies his keen mind and iron will.<br /><br />The Winwood family has title but no money. Rule doesn’t know much about her but decides to marry the eldest</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2858717517358904578">Really interesting characters. Fun scrapes and schemes. I didn’t want to stop reading. I was eager for them to fall in love.<br /><br />STORY BRIEF:<br />I excerpted much of the following from the website Heyerlist dot org which says it well – what to expect when you read this book.<br /><br />The Earl of Rule (Rule) is 35, proud, wealthy. He has a pleasant, mocking, lazy charm which belies his keen mind and iron will.<br /><br />The Winwood family has title but no money. Rule doesn’t know much about her but decides to marry the eldest daughter Elizabeth. Horatia (Horry) is 17 and the younger sister. Horry goes to Rule and tells him Elizabeth loves another and that Horry would like to marry Rule instead. She has heard that men like him have mistresses and Horry assures him she will not interfere with that. Horry admits to Rule her flaws - she has straight, thick black eyebrows, a pronounced stammer, and is short. They marry. Horry is mischievous, honest, frank, high-spirited, and has inherited her family’s tendency to gamble. She gets into numerous scrapes.<br /><br />Three people try to cause problems with the marriage, Rule’s mistress, Lethbridge who wants to hurt Rule in any way he can, and Crosby (Rule’s cousin who is further removed from inheriting Rule’s wealth now that he is married). Pel is Horry’s brother who gambles and drinks too much. Pel plans various schemes to help Horry get out of messes.<br /><br />REVIEWER’S OPINION:<br />I didn’t want to stop reading. I wanted to know what would happen. I loved Horry’s zestful spirit, refreshing honesty, and her roguish charm. Part of the draw was I kept hoping and waiting for Rule and Horry to fall in love. Rule stopped seeing his mistress and I wanted Horry to know about it, but she didn’t. I was chuckling a few times at the ridiculous plans and actions of Horry’s brother Pel trying to help her. Pel’s actions were silly but entertaining. <br /><br />One part is probably more humorous hearing it as an audiobook than reading it. Pel puts on a mask and attempts to rob a horse-drawn carriage. He shoots his gun to stop the horses and yells “Stand and deliver.” The narrator says this with a British accent which was funny. It’s so different from American westerns where the robber says “This is a holdup” or “This is a stickup.”<br /><br />The author is very good with dialogue which a lot of current day authors should do more of.<br /><br />SOUND QUALITY:<br />The narrator Caroline Hunt has a pleasant voice, but the recording was hard to hear – as if too many low tones and not enough treble. At times I had to turn up the volume which was not a good solution. I don’t know if the problem was her voice or the equipment used to record this. I downloaded the version with the best quality audio.<br /><br />CAUTION SPOILER:<br />Horry and Rule finally communicate that they love each other during the last few sentences of the book. I wanted another chapter or epilogue to experience the love and to see their feelings and interactions AFTER that moment. That would have taken it to 5 stars for me.<br /><br />DATA:<br />Unabridged audiobook length: 9 ½ hours. Narrator: Caroline Hunt. Swearing language: none. Sexual content: none. Setting: 1776 England. Book Published: 1934. Genre: historical romance, Georgian romance.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_57419437">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/57419437" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/897073-angela" class="left imgcol" title="Angela"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1219940542p2/897073.jpg" alt="Angela" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/57419437?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 26, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/897073-angela" class="user" title="Angela">Angela</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32106.The_Convenient_Marriage" title="Paperback 9780099474425" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/897073-angela?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/897073-angela?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/897073-angela?shelf=regency" class="actionLinkLite">regency</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer57419437">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer658127474606305832">This plot is almost the same, though rather more fast-paced, than Heyer's "April Lady": Older, rich, eligible bachelor, well-known to have had a mistress, falls almost instantly and surprisingly for a young woman of good family but no fortune (as it has been spent away in gaming, which tendency runs in the family). Girl's mother warns her daughter not to be an affectionate wife, so instead the silly chit is wildly extravagant with her husband's money. She lands in various scrapes and runs to her</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText658127474606305832">This plot is almost the same, though rather more fast-paced, than Heyer's "April Lady": Older, rich, eligible bachelor, well-known to have had a mistress, falls almost instantly and surprisingly for a young woman of good family but no fortune (as it has been spent away in gaming, which tendency runs in the family). Girl's mother warns her daughter not to be an affectionate wife, so instead the silly chit is wildly extravagant with her husband's money. She lands in various scrapes and runs to her reckless, gambling, but well-meaning brother for help (because, of course, she can't confide in her husband), but his solutions - involving jewels, more gambling, and even highwaymen - are all ridiculously unorthodox and eventually unsuccessful. In the end, the heroine realizes that her husband actually does love her and everyone lives happily ever after (is that a spoiler? sorry...this is a romance novel, so I can't imagine there was a question).<br /><br />Being much more up-beat than "April Lady," I enjoyed this version of the same plot slightly more, but I spent most of the book quite out of patience with "Horry" (what a horrible name). She talks of liking her husband very much, but when it comes to treating him like a human being - let alone with any kind of respect or real affection - she fails miserably. Her brother and his friends were funny, but their caprices and drunken scenes became quickly tiresome. Rule was an interesting character, and if it weren't for his stupid, scheming mistress, I would have liked him very much. In the end, it was entertaining enough, but not one I'd rush to pick up again.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="658127474606305832">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_453038336">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/453038336" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/841949-tracey" class="left imgcol" title="Tracey"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1325394892p2/841949.jpg" alt="Tracey" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/453038336?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 20, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/841949-tracey" class="user" title="Tracey">Tracey</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7958128-the-convenient-marriage" title="Audio CD 9781843794417" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/841949-tracey?shelf=3-star" class="actionLinkLite">3-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer453038336">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2240041886866979594">This was my first Georgette Heyer, to which I was irresistibly drawn by the fact that it's an audiobook read by Richard (Thornton Guisborne Thorin) Armitage. Also: Georgette Heyer. All I've ever heard about her is how wonderful her books are, the epitome of their genre, not to be missed. <br /><br />I feel let down. <br /><br />It's a cute idea. Horatia ("Horry") (note to parents everywhere: don't name your child Horatia, or that's what will happen) Winwood sees her older sister Elizabeth being drawn inexorably into a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2240041886866979594">This was my first Georgette Heyer, to which I was irresistibly drawn by the fact that it's an audiobook read by Richard (Thornton Guisborne Thorin) Armitage. Also: Georgette Heyer. All I've ever heard about her is how wonderful her books are, the epitome of their genre, not to be missed. <br /><br />I feel let down. <br /><br />It's a cute idea. Horatia ("Horry") (note to parents everywhere: don't name your child Horatia, or that's what will happen) Winwood sees her older sister Elizabeth being drawn inexorably into a terrible situation: she loves someone else, but the Earl of Rule has asked for her hand. Given the family's financial situation – including a brother who enjoys the drink and the gambling – there is no choice: Elizabeth must marry the rich lord and not her penniless soldier boy. So Horatia – though very young by current standards – takes matters into her own hands. She tromps off to present herself to Rule and – calmly, coolly, and collectedly – offer herself as a substitute. Purely a business arrangement, you understand, and neither of them expected to interfere with the other; he can even keep seeing his mistress. (!) When her mother and sisters find out they all nearly conniption from the horror and embarrassment, but when it turns out that Rule rather liked the audacity of it all things look much brighter. <br /><br />The problem is that the concentration of the story drifts from there into other waters. If it had held its focus on Horry being unconventionally audacious and ahead of her time, convinced that whatever she was starting to feel for him the marriage was one of convenience purely, and so on, I might have had fun. But her unconventionality transmutes into a penchant for gambling and the high life just like her brother's, and it was a little nauseating. She was presented as being a smart girl, and yet she immediately forgets what it was like not to have very much and begins spending money like one to the manner born. Then the whole thing deteriorates into a rather unpleasant farce involving an extremely unwise flirtation with another man leading to results so nearly tragic I was a little stunned; I had expected something light and clever, not this adventure, involving at least two episodes of faux-highway-robbery, near-ravishment, a missing brooch, disuises, and Horry's brother and his Wodehouse-esque goofy sidekick. <br /><br />Armitage did a fine job of reading it – as well, that is, as any man could be expected to do with a book featuring a passel of women in the primary roles, one of whom has – wait for it – a stutter. <br /><br />I have to ask – whoever chose this among all of Heyer's novels – what were they smoking? An audiobook of a novel whose main character <em>stutters?</em> It was painful to listen to – I can only imagine it was painful to narrate. I hope they paid Armitage well. <br /><br />I understand that this is one of Georgette Heyer's early books, and not among the best; also, I just belatedly noticed that the audiobook was (horrors!) abridged. So this won't put me off the author's body of work. <br /><br />Almost. But not quite.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2240041886866979594">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9069193986857490001">"The Viscount stepped into the room. "Came to see if you was dead," he said. "Laid Pom odds you weren't." <br /><em>Lethbridge passed his hand across his eyes. "I'm not," he replied in a faint voice. <br />"No. I'm sorry," said the Viscount simply. He wandered over to the table and sat down. "Horry said she killed you, Pom said So she might, I said No. Nonsense." <br />Lethbridge still holding a hand to his aching head tried to pull himself together. "Did you?" he said. His eyes ran over his self invited guest. "I se</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9069193986857490001">"The Viscount stepped into the room. "Came to see if you was dead," he said. "Laid Pom odds you weren't." <br /><em>Lethbridge passed his hand across his eyes. "I'm not," he replied in a faint voice. <br />"No. I'm sorry," said the Viscount simply. He wandered over to the table and sat down. "Horry said she killed you, Pom said So she might, I said No. Nonsense." <br />Lethbridge still holding a hand to his aching head tried to pull himself together. "Did you?" he said. His eyes ran over his self invited guest. "I see. Let me assure you once more that I am very much alive." <br />"Well I wish you'd put your wig on," complained the Viscount. "What I want to know is why did Horry hit you on the head with a poker?" <br />Lethbridge gingerly felt his bruised scalp. "With a poker was it? Pray ask her, though I doubt if she will tell you." <br />"You shouldn't keep the front door open," said the Viscount. "What's to stop people coming in and hitting you over the head? It's preposterous." <br />"I wish you'd go home," said Lethbridge wearily. <br />The Viscount surveyed the supper-table with a knowing eye. <br />"Card-party?" he inquired knowingly.</em> <br /><br /><br />This book features on of the few Heyer heroines who doesn't annoy me at some point or another! Horry Winwood. The girl: stammers, has ugly big eyebrows, is really short, rude, and likes to drink and gamble. She marries the Earl because her family needs the money, and her older sister, who was to be the "Sacrifice," to him, is in love with someone else. The Earl is one of Heyer's perfect models of wit, good breeding, excellent taste, a fine, if hidden mind, and a way of handling every situation near perfectly. His only flaws are of laziness and far too much indulgence of his young wife. Which is more than enough for Horry! She manages to make lots of trouble for herself, thoroughly manipulated by the villain of the piece, a man looking for revenge upon her husband.<br /><br />I found Horry adorable, loved the Earl, and though you want to shake both of them at various times, it isn't in a 'you're annoyingly, badly written' sort of way. You're supposed to want to shake them, its part of the book drawing you in. I don't know if I really believe that someone like the Earl would fall in love with a silly seventeen year old girl, but I rather enjoyed suspending my disbelief on that.<br /><br />Also? I love Pel! Short of Rupert in These Old Shades, he's my favorite supporting cast member/plot mover in Heyer's romances.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_114058155">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/114058155" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3015503-maria-grazia" class="left imgcol" title="Maria Grazia"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1347724212p2/3015503.jpg" alt="Maria Grazia" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/114058155?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 13, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3015503-maria-grazia" class="user" title="Maria Grazia">Maria Grazia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/7958128-the-convenient-marriage" title="Audio CD 9781843794417" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3015503-maria-grazia?shelf=read-in-2010" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer114058155">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17374946303978589122">You put your CD in the player, push the play button to make it start and when the caressing voice comes out and begins to tell you the story … you can’t really concentrate on the words and their meaning . It’s just a pleasant mind/body sensation totally out of meaning. So when you realize the story has gone on and you didn’t catch much of it , you pause the CD, try to convince yourself you must act your age and behave sensibly, try to remind yourself of Georgette Heyer’s mastery on wit , romp an</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17374946303978589122">You put your CD in the player, push the play button to make it start and when the caressing voice comes out and begins to tell you the story … you can’t really concentrate on the words and their meaning . It’s just a pleasant mind/body sensation totally out of meaning. So when you realize the story has gone on and you didn’t catch much of it , you pause the CD, try to convince yourself you must act your age and behave sensibly, try to remind yourself of Georgette Heyer’s mastery on wit , romp and romance and , finally, you start it over again. You concentrate on the skillful reading and characterization of the talented reader (trying to think of his penetrating blue eyes and gorgeous look), on the intriguing tones of his voice but also on his involving conveying the entertaining story in his elegant Northern – British accent and… you find yourself totally immersed in 5 hours of heavenly delight. A delight you want to prolong and are sad to be parted from after the last incredibly romantic moments are over. I shivered from head to toes at listening to those deep seductive whispers in which Lord Rule teases young Horatia revealing at the same time all his love and admiration for her. <br />OMG! This is not the proper way to start a review of Georgette Heyer’s THE CONVENIENT MARRIAGE However, I hope you’ll forgive my informal , atypical review since Richard Armitage and Georgette Heyer together can stir my enthusiam! Richard Armitage is the alluring, mesmerizing reader of this Naxos Audiobook, abridged version of Heyer’s novel. “Richard Armitage couldn’t be a better choice for reader” was written in a review of his SYLVESTER ( again Georgette Heyer, again Naxos Audiobook) and that is so TRUE! You say I’m biased? Definitely YES! But not of totally unsound mind! Richard Armitage is incredibly good at using his voice to give life to an incredible parade of convincing characters, from young, brave, a bit naive Horatia with her stammer to funny, adventuresque Pel and Pom, from delicate, beautiful Elizabeth Winwood to gallant, treacherous Lethbridge. How can he be so good at remembering all those different voices in his mind and avoid being confused? But in my mind he was Lord Marcus Rule. Precisely Rule had his tall, dark, hansome appearance in my mind and his voice perfectly matched the enigmatic, attractive Heyer hero. <br />Do you think I should say something about the story? I think I’d better say as little as I can. <br />But if you asked me , I ‘d just say - hoping you wouldn’t take it as a spoiler, that the convenient marriage of the title takes place in the first pages, while in many other novels , the marriage or the proposal are the climax. I ‘d add that there are very hilarious moments, tricks, duels, adventures, flirts, highwaymen’s hold ups , a quest for a disappeared brooch and to save the reputation of a lady and , of course, very romantic scenes. <br />My advice is, however, try to read the book, if you can, before you listen to the audiobook. I did it while coping with the “hard task” of listening and ...it took me more time. I fragmented, diluted the pleasure, which is not always negative. I noticed they had cut a lot from the original version, maybe too much for Heyer fans (entire scenes and characters, for instance) , so I stopped the CD and read the book instead. Then I re-started listening and... so on. It also happened that I got lost in the world created by Richard with only his voice and forgot I had my paperback in my hand! The best thing would be to read before, then listening to the CDs. <br />(My printed copy of The Convenient Marriage <a title="The Convenient Marriage by Georgette Heyer" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32106.The_Convenient_Marriage">
  <img class="escapedImg" alt="The Convenient Marriage by Georgette Heyer" src="http://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/books/1168335982s/32106.jpg" /></a>)</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17374946303978589122">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer16316751110024530776">Not my favourite of the Heyer romances I've read so far, but different because it nigh on begins with the couple getting married, and the romance comes later. Also full of sword fights and highwaymen and mistaken identities -- it probably has the most action of Heyer's romances that I've read so far, except maybe The Talisman Ring.<br /><br />I'm not sure why, then, I didn't like it as much as the others. It's still funny, though maybe not as funny as the others, and Horry's brother is quite ridiculous -- t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16316751110024530776">Not my favourite of the Heyer romances I've read so far, but different because it nigh on begins with the couple getting married, and the romance comes later. Also full of sword fights and highwaymen and mistaken identities -- it probably has the most action of Heyer's romances that I've read so far, except maybe The Talisman Ring.<br /><br />I'm not sure why, then, I didn't like it as much as the others. It's still funny, though maybe not as funny as the others, and Horry's brother is quite ridiculous -- too much to be believed, perhaps. It's more slapstick than the witty banter of some of Heyer's other characters.<br /><br />Still, this was plenty of fun, even if I had no doubt how it would end.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_885132474">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/885132474" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/10885890-mullgirl" class="left imgcol" title="Mullgirl"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1415988027p2/10885890.jpg" alt="Mullgirl" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/885132474?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 19, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10885890-mullgirl" class="user" title="Mullgirl">Mullgirl</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32106.The_Convenient_Marriage" title="Paperback 9780099474425" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/10885890-mullgirl?shelf=historical-romance" class="actionLinkLite">historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer885132474">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2088800275649664360">Hmmm. I’m supposed to like this. I’ve been told by countless Austen fans that Heyer is too fab for words. Lovely, lovely regency romances. This was my first Heyer book, and I have to say that The Convenient Marriage was not in fact too fab for words.<br /><br />I was mildly entertained, but ultimately disappointed with the lack of character development and relationship development between the main characters. The 35 year old rake decides it’s time to get hitched. The would-be bride has someone else in mind,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2088800275649664360">Hmmm. I’m supposed to like this. I’ve been told by countless Austen fans that Heyer is too fab for words. Lovely, lovely regency romances. This was my first Heyer book, and I have to say that The Convenient Marriage was not in fact too fab for words.<br /><br />I was mildly entertained, but ultimately disappointed with the lack of character development and relationship development between the main characters. The 35 year old rake decides it’s time to get hitched. The would-be bride has someone else in mind, but of course, her noble family while still enjoying the benefits of a good name has a ne’er do well heir spending the family money, necessitating her marrying the rake. Her much younger sister decides to sacrifice herself instead and offers her to the rake–who for some reason takes her on. Through the wrong character’s eyes (in other words, people who could not possibly know what they know about other people’s thinking) we find out that he “needed” to marry into their family–but we never relaly understand why, and that he fell for the youngest sister–who knows when or why. She evidently takes a shine to him, again, why–who knows–we’re never told.<br /><br />Both characters are fairly likable, especially the rake. He has an interesting manner of seeming relaxed and laissez-faire and flippant while really being in complete control at all times. Sadly, there are likely less than 20 pages of the book where the rake and the sister interact. So you can’t see why they like each other for themselves either.<br /><br />It was too long for what it was, too many plot turns that didn’t add to the pleasure of the read, too little discussing “the convenient marriage.”<br /><br />All that said, there were a few passages that were very well-done and made me want to keep reading. .<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2088800275649664360">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_170534825">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170534825" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3462893-rosanne-lortz" class="left imgcol" title="Rosanne Lortz"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442503803p2/3462893.jpg" alt="Rosanne Lortz" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/170534825?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 24, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3462893-rosanne-lortz" class="user" title="Rosanne Lortz">Rosanne Lortz</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32106.The_Convenient_Marriage" title="Paperback 9780099474425" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer170534825">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13691417360842652467">If you’re looking to read something unpredictable, Georgette Heyer books are not for you. Thirty-something-year-old former rake falls in love with young girl barely out of the schoolroom (or alternatively, with a spunky twenty-something-year-old “spinster”), and after many misunderstandings, much wearing of finery, probably some gambling over cards, perhaps a duel or two, and loads of witty banter, the two finally come to an understanding.<br /><br />Which book is this the plot to? It could be almost any of</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13691417360842652467">If you’re looking to read something unpredictable, Georgette Heyer books are not for you. Thirty-something-year-old former rake falls in love with young girl barely out of the schoolroom (or alternatively, with a spunky twenty-something-year-old “spinster”), and after many misunderstandings, much wearing of finery, probably some gambling over cards, perhaps a duel or two, and loads of witty banter, the two finally come to an understanding.<br /><br />Which book is this the plot to? It could be almost any of the Heyer canon. Of course, there always are the subtle variations, such as the heroine being the first to fall in love with the hero or–egads!–the hero NOT being a former rake. But all in all, Heyer books have transparent plots with markedly similar storylines.<br /><br />Do I mean this as a criticism? Absolutely not! I love picking up a Heyer book because I already know for a fact that I am going to like it (because, yes, I like that kind of plot). Even though I know what’s going to happen, it’s always a delight to experience the subtle plot variations and the new cast of characters along the way.<br /><br />My two favorite Heyer novels, Cotillion and Friday’s Child, both have a plot where the protagonists fall in love with each other AFTER they are engaged/married. I adore how the hero and heroine grow to know each other, see the beauty of each other’s character, and eventually fall in love. I also love the emphasis on MARRIAGE in these books (and in all of Heyer’s books). Heyer, although turning an indulgent eye to youthful follies, is no friend to extramarital affairs. Whatever the hero might have done in his past life, true love comes when he finds it with his wife.<br /><br />When I saw (while scanning Goodreads) that The Convenient Marriage has the same plot as the above mentioned books, how could I not rush to reserve it at the library? The setting of this book is earlier than most Heyer novels–in the Georgian period (the war in the Americas is mentioned a couple times)–so we have the added delight of powdered wigs and emerald-encrusted shoes.<br /><br />When the wealthy Earl of Rule decides to marry the eldest Miss Elizabeth Winwood, she tearfully realizes she must accept. Her brother’s gambling has put the whole family on the brink of ruin, and a rich marriage is the only way to mend matters. Unfortunately for Elizabeth, she is already in love with Edward Heron–a fact she must learn to forget, it seems.<br /><br />In order to save Elizabeth from becoming the Family Sacrifice, her youngest sister Horatia (Horry) Winwood takes matters into her own hands. Approaching the Earl with astonishing audacity, she suggests that he marry her instead. Even though she is not as pretty as her sister, she insists that the marriage will be more agreeable to him since it will be solely a marriage of convenience–which, after all, is what the earl is looking for. The smooth-spoken Rule is quite taken with this stammering, black-browed chit just out of the schoolroom. He agrees to her preposterous proposal and Horry, to the confusion of the watching world, takes her place as the new Countess of Rule.<br /><br />Horry’s unorthodox behavior takes the society world by storm. She gains scores of admirers, spends thousands on new finery, and racks up huge gambling debts which Rule indulgently settles. But when she begins to favor Rule’s long time enemy, Lord Lethbridge, the Earl realizes two things: first, he must take steps to guard his wife from Lethbridge’s foul schemes; and second, the outspoken Horatia Winwood is indeed a treasure worth guarding. Full of duels, abductions, plots, and counterplots, The Convenient Marriage is a fun romp of the first order.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13691417360842652467">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer745536957">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9270167308817247936">Such a fun story! The Convenient Marriage was not what I expected but I enjoyed it a lot! I liked Lord Rule right off the bat but it took me a good bit of the book to get used to Horry. By the end though I couldn't help but like her and I felt like she had hope of maturing haha. The story dragged a bit at times but the parts with Rule and the very sweet ending made up for that. Or course, I did not like the part that Caroline Massey played in the story (early on) as it couldn't help but lower my</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9270167308817247936">Such a fun story! The Convenient Marriage was not what I expected but I enjoyed it a lot! I liked Lord Rule right off the bat but it took me a good bit of the book to get used to Horry. By the end though I couldn't help but like her and I felt like she had hope of maturing haha. The story dragged a bit at times but the parts with Rule and the very sweet ending made up for that. Or course, I did not like the part that Caroline Massey played in the story (early on) as it couldn't help but lower my opinion of Rule, even though that kind of behavior was I guess somewhat common. =/ Over all though, The Convenient Marriage ranks as one of my favorite of Heyer's (so far!) <br />Spoiler: <br />I liked the fact that Heyer gave us little glances throughout the story of Rule and Horry's growing affection for each other. As always, I wouldn't have minded a bit more emphasis on this but their kiss at the end made me happy. =) I also liked Rule's response to Crosby when Crosby visits him about the brooch... what a great scene. I loved Rule's passionate and violent defense of his wife... it reminded me a bit of Percy in some of the Scarlet Pimpernel books. =)</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_728470104">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/728470104" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/19799133-maria" class="left imgcol" title="Maria"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1382981396p2/19799133.jpg" alt="Maria" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/728470104?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 26, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/19799133-maria" class="user" title="Maria">Maria</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/8270023-the-convenient-marriage" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/19799133-maria?shelf=georgette-heyer" class="actionLinkLite">georgette-heyer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer728470104">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6935318842072087372">Horatia Winwood is not a beautiful girl but she has a great heart. She sacrifices herself by marrying the Earl of Rule to save her family from financial ruin and most of all to help her eldest sister, deeply in love with a simple lieutenant, to escape a marriage without love. Moreover, to persuade Lord Rule, she promises not to interfere in his affairs. Can a marriage of convenience turn into a marriage of love? Sometimes it can. Only if you marry the fascinating Earl of Rule, though.<br /><br />It is clear</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6935318842072087372">Horatia Winwood is not a beautiful girl but she has a great heart. She sacrifices herself by marrying the Earl of Rule to save her family from financial ruin and most of all to help her eldest sister, deeply in love with a simple lieutenant, to escape a marriage without love. Moreover, to persuade Lord Rule, she promises not to interfere in his affairs. Can a marriage of convenience turn into a marriage of love? Sometimes it can. Only if you marry the fascinating Earl of Rule, though.<br /><br />It is clear from the first encounter between Horatia and Lord Rule that he is a very charming man. Not only is he a noble man because of his title but he is noble in his manners. He perfectly knows how to behave, how to be an excellent gentleman. I liked his wit but I was impressed especially by his perspicacity. Every time there was a secret about his wife, his friends, his enemies, he was surprisingly the first person to know everything, although he was supposed to be in the dark. I loved all the scenes with Horatia. He was always very sweet and thoughtful to her, even when she did not deserve it. I believe he fell in love with her immediately, the first time he met her. On the other hand I did not like Horatia, at least not soon. She is too careless towards everything. She does not respect her husband and his money. Her only interests are parties, dresses, jewelry and gambling. This cannot be excused by saying that she married him without love, because she behaves like a spoiled girl and sometimes this is annoying. I can understand her just because of her age. At seventeen it is difficult to be wise but fortunately it is not impossible to find a discreet girl of that age.<br /><br />I really found so much hilarious Pelham Winwood, Horatia’s brother, and his friend Roland Pommeroy, often mentioned in the book as Pel and Pom. They are very funny and all the scenes with them are uproarious. My favourite was the duel scene with Crosby Drelincourt, cousin and presumptive heir of Lord Rule. Both Pel and Pom are great characters and give to the story amusement and light heartedness. I enjoyed them a lot. Besides, Pel is quite dashing!<br /><br />The only thing I did not like, but it depends on the fact that I do not like very much the eighteenth century fashion, is men wearing wigs. I cannot imagine that! All the make-up and false moles are not at all enjoyable to me. But, after all, I am a Regency girl.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6935318842072087372">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_42651690">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/42651690" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1893656-delaina" class="left imgcol" title="Delaina"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1445063087p2/1893656.jpg" alt="Delaina" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/42651690?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 11, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1893656-delaina" class="user" title="Delaina">Delaina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32106.The_Convenient_Marriage" title="Paperback 9780099474425" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Jane Austen fans</span></div>

        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer42651690">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17649682840788063762">Heyer is the queen of English Regency romances -- fans of Jane Austen movies who can't quite get a handle on her novels can read the novels of La Georgette and gain a wealth of context and insights into the era. I absolutely adored this story, and for a long time it was my favorite Heyer. The set-up goes like this: <br />Headstrong and outspoken (despite a stammer) 17-year-old Horatia saves her two elder sisters from sacrificing themselves upon the marriage altar for the good of the family. Her family</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17649682840788063762">Heyer is the queen of English Regency romances -- fans of Jane Austen movies who can't quite get a handle on her novels can read the novels of La Georgette and gain a wealth of context and insights into the era. I absolutely adored this story, and for a long time it was my favorite Heyer. The set-up goes like this: <br />Headstrong and outspoken (despite a stammer) 17-year-old Horatia saves her two elder sisters from sacrificing themselves upon the marriage altar for the good of the family. Her family has a "fatal addiction" to gambling and is therefore quite strapped for money; the Earl needs to settle down with a suitably respectable girl of the haute ton. Horatia takes it upon herself to propose marriage to her sister's 35-year-old suitor--who raises an amused eyebrow and urbanely agrees to the new arrangement. Thus begin the adventures of a flighty young woman who falls deeply in love with her worldly husband, and fears he could never love her. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17649682840788063762">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12831494413957520364">Another comedy of errors from Miz Heyer. The constant misunderstandings make this one definitely not in my top 5 Heyer novels, but it's engaging nonetheless. Richard Armitage's excellent narration adds a lot of humour, especially when narrating some of the supporting characters.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer208992562">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2657911284575646103">Hilarious! I can't stop laughing over "Pel" and "Pom"... their antics! The Earl is delightfully droll - reminds me a bit of The Scarlet Pimpernel, the way he pretends to be one thing and is quite another. And the heroine, "Horry" Horatia! At times, I felt Horry ought to be spanked, and at other times, she awed me with her boldness (especially for that day).<br /><br />It's quite an improbable plot. Even more improbable that a man such as the Earl would agree to marry Horatia, no matter how delicious the gos</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2657911284575646103">Hilarious! I can't stop laughing over "Pel" and "Pom"... their antics! The Earl is delightfully droll - reminds me a bit of The Scarlet Pimpernel, the way he pretends to be one thing and is quite another. And the heroine, "Horry" Horatia! At times, I felt Horry ought to be spanked, and at other times, she awed me with her boldness (especially for that day).<br /><br />It's quite an improbable plot. Even more improbable that a man such as the Earl would agree to marry Horatia, no matter how delicious the gossip. Of course the reader knows that the Earl will genuinely fall for her, as she genuinely falls for him. And despite all that improbability, it's quite an enchanting tale!</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");

      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }
  }

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/18067.Georgette_Heyer">About Georgette Heyer</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/18067.Georgette_Heyer"><img alt="18067" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1336748892p2/18067.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer5523779871280768188">Georgette Heyer was a prolific historical romance and detective fiction novelist. Her writing career began in 1921, when she turned a story for her younger brother into the novel <a title=" The Black Moth" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311322._The_Black_Moth"> The Black Moth</a>.<br /><br />In 1925 she married George Ronald Rougier, a mining engineer, and he often provided basic plot outlines for her thrillers. Beginning in 1932, Heyer released one romance novel and one thriller each year.<br /><br />Hey</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5523779871280768188">Georgette Heyer was a prolific historical romance and detective fiction novelist. Her writing career began in 1921, when she turned a story for her younger brother into the novel <a title=" The Black Moth" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311322._The_Black_Moth"> The Black Moth</a>.<br /><br />In 1925 she married George Ronald Rougier, a mining engineer, and he often provided basic plot outlines for her thrillers. Beginning in 1932, Heyer released one romance novel and one thriller each year.<br /><br />Heyer was an intensely private person who remained a best selling author all her life without the aid of publicity. She made no appearances, never gave an interview and only answered fan letters herself if they made an interesting historical point. She sometimes wrote under the pseudonym Stella Martin.<br /><br />Her Regencies were inspired by <a title=" Jane Austen" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1265._Jane_Austen"> Jane Austen</a>, but unlike Austen, who wrote about and for the times in which she lived, Heyer was forced to include copious information about the period so that her readers would understand the setting. While some critics thought her novels were too detailed, others considered the level of detail to be Heyer's greatest asset.<br /><br />Heyer remains a popular and much-loved author, known for essentially establishing the historical romance genre and its subgenre Regency romance.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5523779871280768188">...more</a>

    </div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/3183163-the-convenient-marriage">Quotes from The Convenient Ma...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“The Viscount stepped into the room. "Came to see if you was dead," he said. "Laid Pom odds you weren't."<br />Lethbridge passed his hand across his eyes. "I'm not," he replied in a faint voice.<br />"No. I'm sorry," said the Viscount simply. He wandered over to the table and sat down. "Horry said she killed you, Pom said So she might, I said No. Nonsense."<br />Lethbridge still holding a hand to his aching head tried to pull himself together. "Did you?" he said. His eyes ran over his self invited guest. "I see. Let me assure you once more that I am very much alive."<br />"Well I wish you'd put your wig on," complained the Viscount. "What I want to know is why did Horry hit you on the head with a poker?"<br />Lethbridge gingerly felt his bruised scalp. "With a poker was it? Pray ask her, though I doubt if she will tell you."<br />"You shouldn't keep the front door open," said the Viscount. "What's to stop people coming in and hitting you over the head? It's preposterous."<br />"I wish you'd go home," said Lethbridge wearily.<br />The Viscount surveyed the supper-table with a knowing eye.<br />"Card-party?" he inquired.”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/65089-the-viscount-stepped-into-the-room-came-to-see-if" class="actionLinkLite">37 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“I see,' agreed Rule. 'You are going to be the Sacrifice.'<br /><br />She looked up at him rather shyly. 'It c-can't signify to you, can it? Except that I know I'm not a Beauty, like L-Lizzie. But I have got the Nose, sir.'<br /><br />Rule surveyed the Nose. 'Undoubtedly, you have the Nose,' he said.<br /><br />Horatia seemed determined to make a clean breast of her blemishes. 'And p-perhaps you could become used to my eyebrows?'<br /><br />The smile lurked at the back of Rule's eyes. 'I think, quite easily.'<br /><br />She said sadly: 'They won't arch, you know. And I ought to't-tell you that we have quite given up hope of my g-growing any taller.'<br /><br />'It would certainly be a pity if you did,' said his lordship.<br /><br />'D-do you think so?' Horatia was surprised. 'It is a great trial to me, I can assure you.' She took a breath, and added, with difficulty: 'You m-may have n-noticed that I have a - a stammer.'<br /><br />'Yes, I had noticed,' the Earl answered gently.<br /><br />'If you f-feel you c-can't bear it, sir, I shall quite understand,' Horatia said in a small, anxious voice.<br /><br />'I like it,'said the Earl.”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/1228295-i-see-agreed-rule-you-are-going-to-be-the" class="actionLinkLite">14 likes</a>
            </nobr>
